The Ruling on Intensification of Oath (Taghliz al-Yamin)
Ruling on oath intensification with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taghliz al-yamin and identify the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Intensification of an oath by time or place is not obligatory; a Muslim's oath is valid as is.

This passage from al-Quduri addresses a common question: must an oath be taken at a specific place (like the minbar) or time to be binding? The Hanafi school clarifies that no such intensification is required for a Muslim. The author provides two hadiths to support this, one from Jabir ibn Abdullah about the severity of false oaths at the minbar, which actually indicates that swearing there is not required.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the clear legal statement: intensification of the oath is not obligatory in time or place.
The Arabic phrase 'لا يجب تغليظ اليمين على المسلم بزمان ولا بمكان' is the ruling.
2
Identify the first dalil
Find the hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah about swearing at the Prophet's minbar.
The hadith is from Sunan Ibn Majah.
3
Analyze wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling: it warns against false oaths at the minbar but does not command swearing there, indicating it is not obligatory.
The threat for false oaths applies generally, not as a requirement to swear there.
4
Identify the second dalil
Note the partial hadith from Abu Hurayrah about three people Allah will not speak to, which includes a false oath.
This reinforces the sinfulness of false oaths without mandating a specific location.
5
Conclude the ruling
Synthesize: The proofs support that intensification is not obligatory; a Muslim's oath is complete without it.
The Hanafi position is that taghliz is mubah (permissible) but not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۵ وَلَا يَجِبُ تَغْلِيظُ الْيَمِينِ عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِ بِزَمَانٍ وَلَا بِمَكَانٍ
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجِبُ تَغْلِيظُ الْيَمِينِ عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِ 
عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ حَلَفَ بِيَمِينِ اثْمَةٍ عِنْدَ مِنْبَرِي هَذَا، فَلْيَتَبَوَّأْ مَقْعَدَهُ مِنَ النَّارِ، وَلَوْ عَلَى سِوَاكِ أَخْضَرَ» (سنن ابن ماجه ، بَابُ الْيَمِينِ عِنْدَ مَقَاطِعِ الحقُوقِ نمبر2325/)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يَجِبُ تَغْلِيظُ الْيَمِينِ عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِ 
عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «ثَلَاثَةٌ لَا يُكَلِّمُهُمُ اللَّهُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ، رَجُلٌ مَنَعَ ابْنَ السَّبِيلِ فَضْلَ مَاءٍ عِنْدَهُ، وَرَجُلٌ حَلَفَ ...
35. And intensification of the oath is not obligatory for the Muslim in time or place. Face (1): the hadith for establishing... from Jabir ibn 'Abdullah that the Prophet said: 'Whoever takes a sinful oath at this pulpit of mine, let him take his seat in the Fire, even if it be over a green twig.' Face (2): the hadith for establishing... from Abu Hurayrah that the Prophet said: 'Three people Allah will not speak to on the Day of Resurrection: a man who withholds surplus water from a traveler, and a man who swore...' (incomplete)
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of tawghlith (intensification) of the oath. The Hanafi ruling is that it is not obligatory for a Muslim to have the oath administered in a specific place (like the mosque) or time (like after prayer). The first hadith from Jabir mentions the severity of swearing falsely at the Prophet's minbar, but this does not mean it is required; rather, it warns against false oaths. The second hadith from Abu Hurayrah, though incomplete, indicates that false oath is a major sin. The general principle is that a Muslim's oath is valid by simply swearing by Allah, without special intensification.

Key Terms
تغليظ اليمين (taghliz al-yamin): Intensification of the oath by specifying a time or place (e.g., at the pulpit, after prayer) to increase its solemnity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, is taghliz al-yamin wajib?
A) Yes, always.
B) No, it is not obligatory.
C) Only if the claim involves property.
D) Only if the claimant requests it.

Key Takeaway
A Muslim's oath is valid without any temporal or spatial intensification; the hadith warnings about false oaths at the minbar do not imply an obligation to swear there.

Rulings on Division of Joint Property: Intra-Hanafi Disputes and Conditions for Compulsory Division
Legal rulings on division of joint property with intra-Hanafi disagreements and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on compulsory division of joint property: state the fee rule, conditions for granting division, and identify when division is prohibited due to harm.

Core Idea
Compulsory division is allowed only if no harm results; fee distribution follows the Sahibayn's proportional rule.

When co-owners disagree, can one compel division? Hanafi fiqh balances the right to separate shares with the principle of avoiding harm. This lesson unpacks the detailed rulings from Kitab al-Qisma, including the intra-Hanafi debate on division fees and the conditions under which a judge may order division.

Guided Path
1
State the fee dispute
Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa says fee per capita; Sahibayn say proportional to shares. Then identify the proofs: the narration from Ali and the principle of fairness.
The mufta bihi is proportional (Sahibayn).
2
Analyze proof requirements for inherited property
Note that Abu Hanifa requires proof of death and number of heirs for real estate; Sahibayn accept admission. For movables, all agree division can proceed on claim.
The hadith 'la darar' and Umar's letter are cited.
3
Apply benefit vs harm scenarios
Determine when division is obligatory (all benefit), optional (one harmed but large share), or prohibited (both harmed). Use the hadith 'la darar' and 'la ta'diyah'.
If both harmed, no division without mutual consent.
4
Identify special properties
State that slaves and jewels are not dividable per Abu Hanifa; bathhouse, well, mill not dividable without consent. For goods of same type, division is allowed.
The hadith on freeing a share in a slave is used.
5
Handle absent heirs
When present heirs prove inheritance, judge divides and appoints agent for absent. If buyers or absent in possession, no division. Base on Quran 4:58 and principle of justice.
One heir present is insufficient.

ولا يُخبِرُ الْقَاضِي النَّاسَ عَلَى قَاسِم وَاحِدٍ وَلا يَتْرُكُ الْقُسَّامَ يَشْتَرَكُونَ وَأُجْرَةُ الْقِسْمَةِ عَلَى عَدَدِ الرُّءُوسِ عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ عَلَى قَدْرِ الْأَنْصِبَاءِ
وَإِذَا حَضَرَ الشُرَكَاءُ عِنْدَ الْقَاضِي وَفِي أَيْدِيهِمْ دَارٌ أَوْ ضَيْعَةُ ادَّعَوْا أَنَّهُمْ وَرِثُوهَا عَنْ فُلَانٍ لَمَّ يَقْسِمُهَا الْقَاضِي عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ حَتَّى يُقِيمُوا الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى مَوْتِهِ وَعَدَدِ وَرَثَتِهِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ: يَقْسِمُهَا بِاعْتِرَافِهِمْ وَيَذْكُرُ فِي كِتَابِ الْقِسْمَةِ أَنَّهُ قَسَمَهَا بِقَوْلِهِمْ
ه وَإِذَا كَانَ الْمَالُ الْمُشْتَرَكُ مِمَّا سِوَى الْعَقَارِ ادَّعَوْا أَنَّهُمْ وَرِثُوهُ قَسَمَهُ فِي قَوْلِهِمْ جَمِيعًا وَإِنْ ادَّعَوْا في الْعَقَارِ أَنَّهُمْ اشْتَرَوْهُ قَسَمَهُ بَيْنَهُمْ وَإِنْ ادَّعَوْا الْمِلْكَ وَلَمْ يَذْكُرُوا كَيْفَ انْتَقَلَ إِلَيْهِمْ قَسَمَهُ بَيْنَهُمْ بِاعْتِرَافِهِمْ
وَإِذَا كَانَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الشَّرَكَاءِ يَنْتَفِعُ بِنَصِيبِهِ قَسَمَ بِطَلَبِ أَحَدِهِمْ
ل وَإِنْ كَانَ أَحَدُهُمْ يَنْتَفِعُ وَالْآخَرُ يَتَضَرَّرُ لِقِلَّةِ نَصِيبِهِ فَإِنْ طَلَبَ صَاحِبُ الْكَثِيرِ قَسَمَ الْعَزِيزِ: «لَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُونَ قَاضِيًا حَتَّى تَكُونَ فِيهِ خَمْسُ خِصَالٍ إِنْ أَخْطَأَتْهُ خَصْلَةٌ، كَانَتْ فِيهِ وَصْمَةٌ، حَتَّى يَكُونَ عَالِمًا بِمَا كَانَ قَبْلَهُ، مُسْتَشِيرًا لِذَوِي الرَّأْيِ، ذَا نُهْيَةٍ عَنِ الطَّمَعِ، حَلِيمًا عَنِ الخصم، مُحْتَمِلًا لِلَّائِمَةِ»، (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَاب كَيْفَ يَنْبَغِي لِلْقَاضِي أَنْ يَكُونَ، نمبر 15287)
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَلا يُخْبِرُ الْقَاضِي النَّاسَ عَلَى قَاسِمِ وَاحِدٍ \ عَنْ مُوسَى بْنِ طَرِيفٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: مَرَّ عَلِيٌّ بِرَجُلٍ يَحْسِبُ بَيْنَ قَوْمٍ بِأَجْرٍ، فَقَالَ لَهُ عَلِيٌّ: «إِنَّمَا تَأْكُلُ سُحْتًا» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ الْأَجْرِ عَلَى تَعْلِيمِ الْعِلْمَانِ وَقِسْمَةِ الْأَمْوَالِ، غمبر 14536) وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِذَا حَضَرَ الشُرَكَاءُ عِنْدَ الْقَاضِي قَالَ: كَتَبَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ إِلَى أَبِي مُوسَى الْأَشْعَرِي ....... الْمُسْلِمُونَ عُدُولٌ بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَى بَعْضٍ،»، (سنن دارقطني كِتَابُ عُمَرَ إِلَى أَبِي مُوسَى الْأَشْعَرِيِّ، نمبر 4471)
د وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ كَانَ أَحَدُهُمْ يَنْتَفِعُ وَالْآخَرُ يَتَضَرَّرُا عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( لَا ضَرَرَوَلَا ضِرَار (سنن ابن ماجه، بَابُ مَنْ بَنَى فِي حَقِّهِ مَا يَضُرُّ بِجَارِهِ، نمبر 2341)
اصول: ہر وہ کام جس سے عوام کو نقصان ہو تا ہو اسے روکنے کی کوشش کرے۔ اصول: منقولی جائداد میں خرابی ہونے کا اندیشہ رہتا ہے، اسلئے بطورِ حفاظت جلدی تقسیم کیا جائے گا۔ اصول: کسی اور کے خلاف فیصلہ صادر نہ ہو تا ہو تو مزید گواہ کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں۔
وَإِنْ طَلَبَ صَاحِبُ الْقَلِيلِ لَمْ يَقْسِمْ ك وَإِذَا كَانَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ يَتَضَرَّرُ لَمْ يَقْسِمْ إِلَّا بِتَرَاضِيهِمَا ، وَيَقْسِمُ الْعُرُوضَ إِذَا كَانَتْ مِنْ صِنْفِ وَاحِدٍ و وَلَا يَقْسِمُ الْخِنْسَانِ بَعْضُهُمَا فِي بَعْضٍ إِلَّا بِتَرَاضِيهِمَا وَقَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ: لَا يَقْسِمُ الرَّقِيقَ وَلَا الْجَوَاهِرَ
ا وَلَا يُقْسَمُ حَمَّامٌ وَلا بِئْرٌ وَلا رَحًا إِلَّا أَنْ يَتَرَاضَى الشَّرَكَاءُ الوَإِذَا حَضَرَ وَارِثَانٍ وَأَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى الْوَفَاةِ وَعَدَدِ الْوَرَثَةِ وَالدَّارُ فِي أَيْدِيهِمْ وَمَعَهُمْ وَارِثٌ غَائِبٌ قَسَمَهَا الْقَاضِي بِطَلَبِ الْحَاضِرِينَ وَنَصَّبَ لِلْغَائِبِ وَكِيلًا يَقْبِضُ نَصِيبَهُ الوَإِذَا كَانُوا مُشْتَرِينَ لَمْ يَقْسِمْ مَعَ غَيْبَةِ أَحَدِهِمْ
وَإِنْ كَانَ الْعَقَارُ فِي يَدِ الْوَارِثِ الْغَائِبِ أَوْ شَيْءٌ مِنْهُ لَمْ يَقْسِمْ وَإِنْ حَضَرَ وَارِثٌ وَاحِدٌ لَمْ يَقْسِمْ وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا كَانَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ يَتَضَرَّرُ \ عَنْ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ - يَعْنِي: ابْنَ حَزْمٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ : " لَا تَعْضِيَةَ عَلَى أَهْلِ الْمِيرَاثِ إِلَّا مَا حَمَلَ الْقَسْمُ ". يَقُولُ: لَا يُبَعْضُ عَلَى الْوَارِثِ قَالَ أَبُو عُبَيْدٍ: قَوْلُهُ: " لَا تَعْضِيَةَ فِي مِيرَاتٍ "، يَعْنِي أَنْ يَمُوتَ الْمَيِّتُ، وَيَدَعَ شَيْئًا، إِنْ قُسَمَ بَيْنَ وَرَثَتِهِ، إِذَا أَرَادَ بَعْضُهُمُ الْقِسْمَةَ كَانَ فِي ذَلِكَ ضَرَرٌ عَلَيْهِ مْ، أَوْ عَلَى بَعْضِهِمْ يَقُولُ: فَلَا يُقَسَّمُ، وَالتَّعْضِيَةُ التَّفْرِيقُ (السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ مَا لَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْقِسْمَةَ، غبر 20447/20446)
وجه : (۱): الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُقْسَمُ حَمَّامٌ وَلَا بِثْرٌ وَلَا رَحًا \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِي اللَّه عنهما : أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «مَنْ أَعْتَقَ شِرَكًا لَهُ فِي عَبْدِ، فَكَانَ لَهُ مَالٌ يَبْلُعُ ثَمَنَ الْعَبْدِ، قَومَ الْعَبْدُ قِيمَةَ عَدْلٍ، فَأَعْطَى شُرَكَاءَهُ حِصَصَهُمْ، وَعَتَقَ عَلَيْهِ، وَإِلَّا فَقَدَ عَتَقَ مِنْهُ مَا عَتَقَ»،(بخاري شريف، بَابٌ : إِذَا أَعْتَقَ عَبْدًا بَيْنَ اثْنَيْنِ أَوْ أَمَةً بَيْنَ الشُّرَكَاءِ، نمبر 2522/مسلم ،نمبر 1501) الوجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَإِذَا حَضَرَ وَارِثَانِ وَأَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى الْوَفَاةِ \ ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَأْمُرُكُمْ أَن تُؤَدُّوا الْأَمَانَاتِ إِلَى أَهْلِهَا وَإِذَا حَكَمْتُم بَيْنَ النَّاسِ أَن تَحْكُمُوا بِالْعَدْلِ إِنَّ اللَّهَ نِعِمَّا يَعِظُكُم به ﴾ (سورة النساء، 4 أيت، نمبر 58)
اصول: جہاں افراز اور تمیز ہو وہاں دونوں کی رضا مندی لازم نہیں ہے، بلکہ ایک کے مطالبہ پر تقسیم ہو سکتی ہے اصول: امام ابو حنیفہ : انسان اور جو اہر میں باطنی خوبی کا فرق ہے۔
اصول: جہاں تقسیم میں دونوں کا نقصان ہو وہاں دونوں کی رضامندی کے بغیر تقسیم نہیں ہو گی.
The judge should not appoint people to a single divider, nor should he leave the dividers to join together (in partnership). The fee for division is according to the number of heads (persons) according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: according to the portions. And when the partners appear before the judge and in their hands is a house or a farm, claiming that they inherited it from so-and-so, the judge does not divide it according to Abu Hanifa until they establish evidence of his death and the number of heirs. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: He divides it by their admission, and he mentions in the book of division that he divided it by their statement. And if the shared property is other than real estate, and they claim they inherited it, he divides it according to all of their statements. If they claim regarding real estate that they bought it, he divides it between them. If they claim ownership without mentioning how it transferred to them, he divides it between them by their admission. And when each of the partners benefits from his share, it is divided at the request of one of them. And if one of them benefits and the other is harmed due to the smallness of his share, then if the one with the large share requests division, the judge [divides]. The noble: 'It is not befitting that a person be a judge unless he possesses five characteristics: if he misses one, there is a defect in him: he should be knowledgeable of what came before him, consultative with people of opinion, have restraint from greed, be forbearing with the opponent, and bear criticism.' (Musannaf Abdur Razzaq, chapter on how a judge should be, no. 15287) Explanation: (1) The saying of the tabi'i to prove: 'The judge should not appoint people to a single divider.' From Musa ibn Tarif, from his father, who said: Ali passed by a man calculating between a people for a fee, and Ali said to him: 'You are only consuming illicit gain.' (Musannaf Abdur Razzaq, chapter on fee for teaching knowledge and division of wealth, no. 14536) Explanation: (1) The saying of the Companion to prove: 'And when the partners appear before the judge...' He said: Umar ibn al-Khattab wrote to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: '...Muslims are reliable, some of them against others.' (Sunan Darqutni, book of Umar's letter to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, no. 4471) Explanation: (1) The hadith to prove: 'And if one of them benefits and the other is harmed.' From Ibn Abbas, who said: The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: 'No harm and no reciprocating harm.' (Sunan Ibn Majah, chapter on one who builds in his right what harms his neighbor, no. 2341) Principles: Every action that causes harm to the public should be prevented. Principle: In movable property, there is fear of damage, so out of precaution it should be divided quickly. Principle: If no judgment is issued against another, there is no need for additional witnesses. And if the owner of the small share requests, it is not divided. And if each of them is harmed, it is not divided except by their mutual consent. He divides goods if they are of one type. And he does not divide two different types in exchange for each other except by their mutual consent. Abu Hanifa said: He does not divide slaves nor jewels. And a bathhouse, a well, and a mill are not divided unless the partners mutually agree. And when two heirs appear and establish evidence of death and the number of heirs, and the house is in their hands, and with them is an absent heir, the judge divides it at the request of those present and appoints an agent for the absent one to take his share. And if they are buyers, he does not divide in the absence of one of them. And if the real estate is in the hand of the absent heir, or part of it, he does not divide. And if only one heir is present, he does not divide. Explanation: (1) The hadith to prove: 'And if each of them is harmed.' From Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr (meaning Ibn Hazm), from his father, from the Prophet (peace be upon him), who said: 'No division upon the heirs except what the division bears.' He says: It is not to be divided upon the heir. Abu Ubayd said: His statement 'No division in inheritance' means that when a person dies and leaves something, if it is divided among his heirs, when some of them want division, there is harm in that for them or for some of them. He says: So it should not be divided. And 'division' means separation. (Sunan al-Kubra lil-Bayhaqi, chapter on what does not bear division, nos. 20447/20446) Explanation: (1) The hadith to prove: 'And a bathhouse, a well, and a mill are not divided.' From Abdullah ibn Umar (may God be pleased with them) that the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever frees his share in a slave, and he has sufficient wealth to reach the value of the slave, the slave is valued at a fair price, then he gives his partners their shares, and the slave is freed. Otherwise, only what he freed is freed.' (Bukhari, chapter: If a slave between two persons or a female slave between partners is freed, no. 2522; Muslim, no. 1501) Explanation: (1) The verse to prove: 'And when two heirs appear and establish evidence of death...' (Quran 4:58): 'Indeed, God commands you to render trusts to whom they are due and when you judge between people to judge with justice. Excellent is what God instructs you. Indeed, God is Hearing and Seeing.' Principle: Where separation and distinction are possible, mutual consent is not necessary; division can be done at the request of one. Principle: Imam Abu Hanifa: There is a difference in inner quality between humans and jewels. Principle: Where division causes harm to both, division is not done without their mutual consent.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Qisma (Book of Division) in al-Quduri's Mukhtasar presents the Hanafi rulings on dividing jointly owned property. The text opens with an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the appointment of a single divider and the fee for division. Abu Hanifa holds that the fee is distributed equally per capita, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say it is proportional to each partner's share. The judge must not restrict people to one divider nor allow the dividers to form a partnership; instead, multiple qualified dividers should be available. The proof offered for the first ruling is a saying of a tabi'i (successor) and a narration from Ali condemning taking a fee for dividing as illicit gain. For the second ruling, the proof is the principle that Muslims are reliable witnesses, as stated in Umar's letter to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. Next, the passage addresses division when partners present a claim of inheritance or purchase. Abu Hanifa requires proof of death and number of heirs for real estate inherited; the Sahibayn accept the partners' admission alone. For movable property or when ownership is claimed without detail, division is permitted based on their admission. The rationale is that in movables, there is risk of damage, so division should be expedited as a protective measure. The passage then deals with scenarios of benefit and harm. If each partner benefits from his share, division is obligatory at the request of one. If one benefits and another is harmed due to a small share, the one with the larger share can compel division. The hadith 'La darar wa la dirar' (no harm and no reciprocating harm) supports this: the division that brings benefit is allowed, while requiring harm is prevented. If both are harmed, no division occurs without mutual consent, as per the hadith 'La ta'diyah 'ala ahl al-mirath' (no division upon heirs) which means compulsory division is forbidden if it causes harm. For goods (urud) of the same type, division is allowed; for different types, only with consent. Abu Hanifa additionally rules that slaves and jewels are not divisible because they have intrinsic variations that make equal division impossible—a principle that human beings and jewels differ in inner quality. Specific properties like bathhouses, wells, and mills are not divisible unless all partners agree, because division would render them useless. Finally, the passage covers division when some heirs are absent. If two heirs are present and prove the death and number of heirs, the judge divides and appoints an agent for the absent one. If they are buyers, absence prevents division. If the absent heir has possession, division is not done. If only one heir is present, division is also not done. The proof for appointing an agent and proceeding with division is the Quranic verse (4:58) commanding judges to render trusts and judge with justice. The overriding principles are: avoid harm, expedite division when movables may perish, and require mutual consent when division causes harm to all.

Key Terms
قسمة (qisma): Division of jointly owned property into shares assigned to each partner.
قاسم (qasim): A person appointed by the judge to physically divide the property and allocate shares.
أجرة القسمة (ujrat al-qisma): The fee paid for the service of dividing the property.
لا ضرر ولا ضرار (la darar wa la dirar): A Prophetic hadith meaning 'No harm and no reciprocating harm', used as a legal maxim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is Abu Hanifa's ruling on the fee for division (ujrat al-qisma)?
A) The fee is divided equally among the partners per capita.
B) The fee is divided proportionally according to each partner's share.
C) The fee is covered by the public treasury.
D) The fee is waived if the partners agree.

Key Takeaway
Compulsory division of joint property is permitted only when no partner is harmed, and the fee for division is paid proportionally to shares (mufta bihi).

Ruling on Contradictory Claims in Division of Property
Three rulings on division disputes: contradictory claims, non-delivery, and third-party claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a partner initially claims full receipt but later contradicts himself, and explain the legal basis for rejecting his claim.

Core Idea
A contradictory claim after division destroys credibility; the opponent's statement with oath governs.

This passage from Kitab al-Qismah addresses a common dispute: one partner changes his story about having received his share. The law treats this contradiction as fatal to his claim, protecting the finality of divisions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contradictory statements
The partner says both 'I received my right fully' and 'I only took part of it.' These statements are mutually inconsistent.
The contradiction is in the degree of receipt.
2
Determine whose statement is trusted
The text states: 'the statement is the statement of his opponent with his oath.' The opponent's version is taken as true.
The opponent must also take an oath.
3
Understand the legal principle
The Urdu commentary explains: a claimant's contradictory statement is not accepted without proof. This is a general evidentiary rule in Hanafi fiqh.
Consistency is a requirement for a credible claim.
4
Apply the ruling
The division remains as originally executed; the partner cannot reopen it based on his later inconsistent claim.
The division is final.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْقِسْمَةِ
٢٢ وَإِنْ قَالَ: اسْتَوْفَيْت حَقِّي ثُمَّ قَالَ : أَخَذْت بَعْضَهُ فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُ خَصْمِهِ مَعَ يَمِينِهِ وَإِنْ قَالَ: أَصَابَنِي إِلَى مَوْضِع كَذَا وَلَمْ يُسَلَّمْهُ إِلَيَّ وَلَمْ يَشْهَدْ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ بِالِاسْتِيفَاءِ وَكَذَّبَهُ شَرِيكُهُ تَخَالَفَا وَفُسِخَتْ الْقِسْمَةُ
۲۴ وَإِذَا اسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضٌ نَصِيبَ أَحَدِهِمَا بِعَيْنِهِ لَمَّ تُفْسَخَ الْقِسْمَةُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَيَرْجِعُ بِحِيَّةِ ذَلِكَ مِنْ نَصِيبٍ شَرِيكِهِ
اصول مدعی کی بات میں تضاد ہو تو بینہ کے بغیر اس کی بات نہیں مانی جائے گی۔
اصول مدعی کی بات میں تضاد نہ ہو اور کسی حرکت سے تقسیم کو تسلیم نہ کیا ہو تو تقسیم توڑی جاسکتی ہے۔
The Book of Division. 22: And if he says: I received my right, then later says: I took part of it, then the statement is the statement of his opponent with his oath. And if he says: it fell to my share in such and such place, and it was not delivered to me, and he did not witness against himself for receipt, and his partner denies him, they dispute and the division is rescinded. 24: And if some thing is claimed as owned (by a third party) from the specific share of one of them, the division is not rescinded according to Abu Hanifa, and he takes compensation for that from the share of his partner. Principle: If the claimant's statement is contradictory, his statement is not accepted without proof. Principle: If the claimant's statement is not contradictory and he did not acknowledge the division by any action, the division may be rescinded.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage from the beginning of Kitab al-Qismah (Book of Division) presents three distinct rulings concerning disputes between partners after a division of joint property. The first ruling (numbered 22) addresses a case where a partner initially claims to have fully received his share, but later contradicts himself by saying he only received part. Because of this contradiction, his word is not accepted; instead, the opposing partner's claim is taken as true, supported by his oath. This follows the legal principle that a contradictory claim by a plaintiff is rejected unless corroborated by evidence. The second ruling deals with a partner who says a specific portion fell to his share but was never delivered to him, and he produces no witness to confirm receipt. The other partner denies this, so there is a dispute; the division is rescinded (faskh) because the delivery is not established. This illustrates the principle that a division is not final until each partner takes possession. The third ruling (numbered 24) presents Abu Hanifa's position: if a third party proves ownership of part of what was allocated to one partner, the division as a whole remains valid. The affected partner does not lose his share; instead, he takes compensation from the other partner's share equivalent to what was taken. Abu Hanifa emphasizes the stability of completed divisions, correcting injustice through compensation rather than nullifying the entire transaction. The Urdu commentary notes the underlying principles: contradictory statements from a plaintiff are unacceptable without proof; non-contradictory statements unaccompanied by any act of acceptance can lead to rescission.

Key Terms
استيفاء (istifā'): Full receipt of one's right or share.
قسمة (qismah): Division of joint property among co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a partner says 'I received my full share' then later says 'I took only part,' the legal outcome is:
A) The division is rescinded.
B) The court accepts the later statement.
C) The other partner's statement with oath is accepted.
D) The property is re-divided.

Key Takeaway
A contradictory claim after division is rejected; the opponent's statement with oath prevails, preserving the division.

Ruling on Non-Delivery and Rescission of Division
Three rulings on division disputes: contradictory claims, non-delivery, and third-party claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a partner claims a specific share fell to him but was not delivered, and explain why the division is rescinded.

Core Idea
Division is not final until delivery; if one partner denies delivery, the division is rescinded.

This second ruling highlights an essential condition for a division's finality: actual delivery of each share. Without it, the division lacks an element of exchange and can be undone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the partner's claim
The partner says a specific portion fell to his share but was never delivered to him. He does not witness against himself that he received it.
He is not admitting receipt.
2
Note the other partner's response
The other partner denies that delivery was made. This creates a dispute.
No admission from either side.
3
Determine the outcome
The text says: 'they dispute and the division is rescinded.' The division is automatically rescinded because delivery is not established.
Rescission occurs without court order? The passage implies automatic rescission.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The Urdu commentary states: if there is no contradiction and no act acknowledging the division, it can be rescinded. Delivery is an act that acknowledges the division.
Non-delivery means the division is incomplete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْقِسْمَةِ
٢٢ وَإِنْ قَالَ: اسْتَوْفَيْت حَقِّي ثُمَّ قَالَ : أَخَذْت بَعْضَهُ فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُ خَصْمِهِ مَعَ يَمِينِهِ وَإِنْ قَالَ: أَصَابَنِي إِلَى مَوْضِع كَذَا وَلَمْ يُسَلَّمْهُ إِلَيَّ وَلَمْ يَشْهَدْ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ بِالِاسْتِيفَاءِ وَكَذَّبَهُ شَرِيكُهُ تَخَالَفَا وَفُسِخَتْ الْقِسْمَةُ
۲۴ وَإِذَا اسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضٌ نَصِيبَ أَحَدِهِمَا بِعَيْنِهِ لَمَّ تُفْسَخَ الْقِسْمَةُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَيَرْجِعُ بِحِيَّةِ ذَلِكَ مِنْ نَصِيبٍ شَرِيكِهِ
اصول مدعی کی بات میں تضاد ہو تو بینہ کے بغیر اس کی بات نہیں مانی جائے گی۔
اصول مدعی کی بات میں تضاد نہ ہو اور کسی حرکت سے تقسیم کو تسلیم نہ کیا ہو تو تقسیم توڑی جاسکتی ہے۔
The Book of Division. 22: And if he says: I received my right, then later says: I took part of it, then the statement is the statement of his opponent with his oath. And if he says: it fell to my share in such and such place, and it was not delivered to me, and he did not witness against himself for receipt, and his partner denies him, they dispute and the division is rescinded. 24: And if some thing is claimed as owned (by a third party) from the specific share of one of them, the division is not rescinded according to Abu Hanifa, and he takes compensation for that from the share of his partner. Principle: If the claimant's statement is contradictory, his statement is not accepted without proof. Principle: If the claimant's statement is not contradictory and he did not acknowledge the division by any action, the division may be rescinded.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of the division, returning property to joint ownership.
قسمة (qismah): Division of joint property among co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a partner says his share was not delivered and the other partner denies, the division is:
A) Upheld because the partner admitted the assignment.
B) Rescinded due to lack of proof of delivery.
C) Converted into a sale.
D) Left for the judge's discretion.

Key Takeaway
A division is rescinded if a partner claims non-delivery and there is no proof or admission of receipt.

Ruling on Third-Party Claim and Compensation in Division
Three rulings on division disputes: contradictory claims, non-delivery, and third-party claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's ruling when a third party proves ownership of part of one partner's specific share after division, and explain the compensation mechanism.

Core Idea
A third-party claim on a divided share does not rescind the division; the affected partner gets compensation from the other partner's share.

This third ruling presents Abu Hanifa's view on a scenario where a completed division is challenged by a third party's ownership claim. Rather than nullifying the division, the law preserves it and provides a remedy through compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
After division, a third party (non-owner) proves that part of what was allocated to one partner actually belongs to them.
The property is 'mustahaqq' (claimed as owned).
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
The division is not rescinded. The affected partner does not lose his share; instead, he takes compensation from the other partner's share.
The compensation equals the value of the claimed portion.
3
Understand the reasoning
Abu Hanifa treats the division as a binding exchange. The partner who received the defective share has a claim for redress, but the overall division stands to preserve stability.
This is based on istihsan (juristic preference) over strict analogy.
4
Contrast with rescission
If the division were rescinded, both parties would revert to joint ownership. Abu Hanifa's ruling avoids that disruption.
Compensation is more practical and just.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْقِسْمَةِ
٢٢ وَإِنْ قَالَ: اسْتَوْفَيْت حَقِّي ثُمَّ قَالَ : أَخَذْت بَعْضَهُ فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُ خَصْمِهِ مَعَ يَمِينِهِ وَإِنْ قَالَ: أَصَابَنِي إِلَى مَوْضِع كَذَا وَلَمْ يُسَلَّمْهُ إِلَيَّ وَلَمْ يَشْهَدْ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ بِالِاسْتِيفَاءِ وَكَذَّبَهُ شَرِيكُهُ تَخَالَفَا وَفُسِخَتْ الْقِسْمَةُ
۲۴ وَإِذَا اسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضٌ نَصِيبَ أَحَدِهِمَا بِعَيْنِهِ لَمَّ تُفْسَخَ الْقِسْمَةُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَيَرْجِعُ بِحِيَّةِ ذَلِكَ مِنْ نَصِيبٍ شَرِيكِهِ
اصول مدعی کی بات میں تضاد ہو تو بینہ کے بغیر اس کی بات نہیں مانی جائے گی۔
اصول مدعی کی بات میں تضاد نہ ہو اور کسی حرکت سے تقسیم کو تسلیم نہ کیا ہو تو تقسیم توڑی جاسکتی ہے۔
The Book of Division. 22: And if he says: I received my right, then later says: I took part of it, then the statement is the statement of his opponent with his oath. And if he says: it fell to my share in such and such place, and it was not delivered to me, and he did not witness against himself for receipt, and his partner denies him, they dispute and the division is rescinded. 24: And if some thing is claimed as owned (by a third party) from the specific share of one of them, the division is not rescinded according to Abu Hanifa, and he takes compensation for that from the share of his partner. Principle: If the claimant's statement is contradictory, his statement is not accepted without proof. Principle: If the claimant's statement is not contradictory and he did not acknowledge the division by any action, the division may be rescinded.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage from the beginning of Kitab al-Qismah (Book of Division) presents three distinct rulings concerning disputes between partners after a division of joint property. The first ruling (numbered 22) addresses a case where a partner initially claims to have fully received his share, but later contradicts himself by saying he only received part. Because of this contradiction, his word is not accepted; instead, the opposing partner's claim is taken as true, supported by his oath. This follows the legal principle that a contradictory claim by a plaintiff is rejected unless corroborated by evidence. The second ruling deals with a partner who says a specific portion fell to his share but was never delivered to him, and he produces no witness to confirm receipt. The other partner denies this, so there is a dispute; the division is rescinded (faskh) because the delivery is not established. This illustrates the principle that a division is not final until each partner takes possession. The third ruling (numbered 24) presents Abu Hanifa's position: if a third party proves ownership of part of what was allocated to one partner, the division as a whole remains valid. The affected partner does not lose his share; instead, he takes compensation from the other partner's share equivalent to what was taken. Abu Hanifa emphasizes the stability of completed divisions, correcting injustice through compensation rather than nullifying the entire transaction. The Urdu commentary notes the underlying principles: contradictory statements from a plaintiff are unacceptable without proof; non-contradictory statements unaccompanied by any act of acceptance can lead to rescission.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istiḥqāq): A third party's successful claim of ownership over property that was divided.
رجوع (rujū'): Recourse or compensation; here meaning the affected partner takes compensation from his partner's share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a third party proves ownership of part of one partner's specific share after division, the division is:
A) Rescinded entirely.
B) Rescinded only for that part.
C) Not rescinded; the affected partner gets compensation.
D) Not rescinded; the affected partner loses his share.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa preserves a completed division even if a third party claims part of a share, providing compensation instead of rescission.

Definition and Condition of Coercion (Ikrah)
Defines ikrah and its key condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ikrah and identify the essential condition for its legal recognition.

Core Idea
Coercion is legally recognized only when the coercer can actually carry out the threat.

This lesson opens the Book of Coercion (Ikrah). The author defines when coercion is legally effective: it must come from someone able to execute the threat, whether a ruler or a robber. Three evidentiary supports are provided: a Quranic verse, a saying of Umar, and a statement of Shurayh. Understanding this condition is crucial for applying ikrah in contracts, divorces, and other legal acts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi definition of ikrah
Recognize that ikrah is compelling another to perform an act under threat of harm. The text defines it as a threat that can be carried out.
The Urdu usool clarifies: 'forcing a person to do something by compulsion is called ikrah.'
2
Identify the essential condition for legal recognition
The coercer must be capable of fulfilling the threatened harm. This condition applies irrespective of whether the coercer is a ruler (sultan) or a common robber (liss).
If the threat cannot be executed, it does not constitute ikrah in Hanafi law.
3
Examine the three proofs provided
The author cites: (1) Quran 24:33 prohibiting compulsion of slave girls, (2) Umar's statement that a man is not trustworthy when starved, bound, or beaten, (3) Shurayh's enumeration of imprisonment, beating, shackling, and threatening as coercion.
These evidences support the condition and scope of ikrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْإِكْرَاهِ قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - الْإِكْرَاهُ يَثْبُتُ حُكْمُهُ إِذَا حَصَلَ مِمَّنْ يَقْدِرُ عَلَى إِيقَاعِ مَا تَوَعَّدَ بِهِ سُلْطَانًا كَانَ أَوْ لِصَّا. وجه: (1) الآية الثبوت الإِكْرَاهُ يَثْبُتُ حُكْمُهُ إِذَا حَصَلَ مِمَّنْ يَقْدِرُ وَلَا تُكْرِهُوا فَتَيَتِكُمْ عَلَى الْبِغَاءِ إِنْ أَرَدْنَ تَحَصُّنَّا، (سورة النور، 24 أيت، نمبر 33) وجه: (۲) قول الصحابى لثبوت الْإِكْرَاهُ يَثْبُتُ حُكْمُهُ إِذَا حَصَلَ مِمَّنْ يَقْدِرُ قَالَ عُمَرُ رضي الله عنه: " لَيْسَ الرَّجُلُ بِأَمِينٍ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ إِذَا جُوّعَتْ، أَوْ أُوثِقَتْ، أَوْ ضُرِبَتْ "، (السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ مَا يَكُونُ إِكْرَاهَا ، نمبر 15107) وجه:(۳) قول التابعى لثبوت الْإِكْرَاهُ يَثْبُتُ حُكْمُهُ إِذَا حَصَلَ مِمَّنْ يَقْدِرُ عَنْ شُرَيْحٍ قَالَ: " الخَبْسُ كُرْهُ، وَالضَّرْبُ كُرْهُ، وَالْقَيْدُ كُرْهُ، وَالْوَعِيدُ كُرَّة "، السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَا يَكُونُ إِكْرَاهَا ، نمبر 15108/مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ طَلَاقِ الْكُرْهِ، نمبر 11424) اصول: کسی شخص پر زبر دستی کر کے کوئی کام کرانے کو اکراہ کہتے ہیں۔
The Book of Coercion. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him -: Coercion's ruling is established when it occurs from one who is able to carry out what he threatened, whether he is a ruler or a robber. Face (1): The verse for establishing coercion's ruling is established when it occurs from one who is able: 'And do not compel your slave girls to prostitution if they desire chastity' (Surah al-Nur, 24:33). Face (2): The saying of the Companion for establishing: Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'A man is not trustworthy over himself when he is starved, or bound, or beaten.' (al-Sunan al-Kubra lil-Bayhaqi, chapter on what constitutes coercion, no. 15107). Face (3): The saying of the Tabi'i for establishing: From Shurayh, he said: 'Imprisonment is coercion, beating is coercion, shackling is coercion, and threatening is coercion.' (al-Sunan al-Kubra lil-Bayhaqi, no. 15108; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on divorce under coercion, no. 11424). Principle: Forcing a person to do something by compulsion is called ikrah.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Coercion. The author defines ikrah as a threat that can be carried out, whether by a ruler (sultan) or a robber (liss). This is a ruling statement. The evidence includes a Quranic verse (24:33) prohibiting coercion of slave girls, showing that coercion is recognized; the saying of Umar that a person is not trustworthy when subjected to starvation, binding, or beating; and the statement of Shurayh that imprisonment, beating, shackling, and threats all constitute coercion. The Urdu usool adds that forcing someone to do something against their will is called ikrah.

Key Terms
إكراه (ikrāh): Coercion under threat of harm by a person capable of carrying out the threat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for coercion (ikrah) to be legally recognized?
A) The threat must come from a ruler only.
B) The coercer must be able to carry out the threat.
C) The victim must be physically harmed.
D) The threat must be written.

Key Takeaway
Ikrah is only valid when the coercer is capable of fulfilling the threat.

Coercion to Destroy Property: The Hanafi Ruling and Its Proof
Ruling on destroying another's property under coercion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on destroying another's property under coercion and identify the coercer as the liable party for damages.

Core Idea
Necessity permits destroying property to save life, but the coercer bears liability.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi fiqh: when a person is forced under threat of death or loss of limb to destroy the property of another Muslim. The ruling balances the principles of darurah (necessity) and daman (liability), allocating responsibility to the coercer rather than the coerced actor. The proof is drawn from the Quranic allowance of carrion under necessity, extended by qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and condition
The act is itlaf (destruction) of a Muslim's property. The condition is coercion under threat of death or loss of a limb. Identify that severe coercion is required.
Lesser threats (e.g. to property) do not apply.
2
State the ruling on permissibility
The coerced person may (yasi'ahu) destroy the property. The act is mubah (permissible) due to necessity.
It is not sinful (la ithma alayhi).
3
Identify liability
The owner has recourse (yudammin) against the coercer (mukrih), not the destroyer. The destroyer was an instrument without free will.
4
Examine the proof
The Quranic verse (2:173) permits carrion under necessity. By qiyas, the same principle extends to permitting destruction of property when life is at stake. The 'illa is darurah.
The dalala is zanni because it is analogical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ أُكْرِهَ عَلَى إِتْلَافِ مَالِ مُسْلِمٍ بِأَمْرٍ يَخَافَ مِنْهُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ أَوْ عَلَى عُضْوٍ مِنْ أَعْضَائِهِ وَسِعَهُ أَنْ يَفْعَلَ ذَلِكَ وَلِصَاحِبِ الْمَالِ أَنْ يُضَمِّنَ الْمُكْرِهَ. ووجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَإِنْ أُكْرِهَ عَلَى إِتْلَافِ مَالِ مُسْلِمٍ بِأَمْرٍ ﴿إِنَّمَا حَرَّمَ عَلَيْكُمُ الْمَيْتَةَ وَالدَّمَ وَلَحْمَ الْخِنزِيرِ وَمَا أُهِلَّ بِهِ لِغَيْرِ اللَّهِ فَمَنِ اضْطُرَّ غَيْرَ بَاغٍ وَلَا عَادٍ فَلَا إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ﴾ (سورة البقرة، 2 آيت نمبر 173)
And if one is coerced to destroy the property of a Muslim by an order he fears for his life or for a limb, it is permissible for him to do that, and the owner of the property may hold the coercer liable. And proof (1) of the verse for establishing coercion to destroy a Muslim's property: 'He has only forbidden to you carrion, blood, the flesh of swine... and whoever is compelled, neither desiring nor transgressing, there is no sin upon him.' (Surah Al-Baqarah 2:173)
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This ruling addresses the destruction of a Muslim's property under coercion. The condition is the same severe threat (life or limb). If coerced by such a threat, the person may destroy the property; he is not sinful. However, the owner has the right to claim compensation (daman) from the coercer, not from the actual destroyer, because the destroyer was an instrument without free will. The proof cited is the same verse from Surah Al-Baqarah that allows consumption of carrion under necessity, extended here by qiyas: just as necessity permits consuming haram, it permits destroying property to save one's life. The owner's recourse is against the coercer because he caused the harm.

Key Terms
إتلاف (itlāf): Destruction or causing damage to property.
مكره (mukrih): The coercer, the one who forces the action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If X is forced at knifepoint to break Y's window, who is liable for the damage according to Hanafi law?
A) X, because he performed the act.
B) Y, for leaving the window vulnerable.
C) The coercer, because he caused the coercion.
D) No one, because it was done under duress.

Key Takeaway
Under Hanafi law, destroying a Muslim's property under severe coercion is permissible with no liability on the destroyer; the coercer must compensate the owner.

Coercion to Disbelief: Conditions for Valid Permission
Hanafi ruling on valid coercion to utter kufr with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for valid coercion (ikrah) to speak kufr and apply the ruling that outward compliance is permissible if the heart remains firm in faith.

Core Idea
Only a threat to life or limb makes outward kufr permissible — the heart must stay firm in iman.

This passage from Kitab al-Ikrah in al-Quduri addresses a critical question: when, if ever, is a Muslim allowed to utter words of disbelief? The answer is not a blanket permission but a carefully delimited concession based on Quran, Sunnah, and the example of the Companions. We will unpack the conditions, the proofs, and the spiritual reward of steadfastness.

Guided Path
1
Define valid ikrah
The text first clarifies what constitutes coercion: only fear of death or loss of limb, not mere imprisonment, chains, or beating.
This is the Hanafi restrictive definition.
2
Identify the permitted act
Under such coercion, the person may outwardly express what is demanded (kufr words) as long as the heart is at peace with faith.
The permission is limited to speech, not inner belief.
3
Note the consequences
If he complies, no sin; if he bears patience until death, he is rewarded.
Steadfastness is superior but not obligatory.
4
Examine the proofs
The author cites Quran 16:106 and the hadith of Ammar ibn Yasir as evidence for the concession.
Both are clear and explicit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الإِكْرَامِ. وَإِنْ أُكْرِهَ عَلَى الْكُفْرِ بِاللَّهِ تَعَالَى أَوْ سَبِّ النَّبيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِحَبْسٍ أَوْ قَيْدٍ أَوْ ضَرْبٍ لَمْ يَكُنْ ذَلِكَ بِإِكْرَاهٍ حَتَّى يُكْرَهَ بِأَمْرِ يَخَافُ مِنْهُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ أَوْ عَلَى عُضْوِ مِنْ أَعْضَائِهِ فَإِذَا خَافَ ذَلِكَ وَسِعَهُ أَنْ يُظْهِرَ مَا أُمِرَ بِهِ فَإِذَا أَظْهَرَ ذَلِكَ وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَئِنٌ بِالْإِيمَانِ فَلَا إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ صَبَرَ حَتَّى قُتِلَ وَلَمْ يُظْهِرِ الْكُفْرَ كَانَ مَأْجُورًا. تَوْجِيهٌ: (1) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ: {وَمَن كَفَرَ بِاللَّهِ مِن بَعْدِ إِيمَانِهِ إِلَّا مَنْ أُكْرِهَ وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَئِنٌ بِالْإِيمَانِ وَلَكِن مَّن شَرَحَ بِالْكُفْرِ صَدْرًا فَعَلَيْهِمْ غَضَبٌ مِّنَ اللَّهِ وَلَهُمْ عَذَابٌ عَظِيمٌ} (سورة النحل: 106) وَجْهٌ: (2) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: عَنْ أَبِي عُبَيْدَةَ بْنِ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ عَمَّارِ بْنِ يَاسِرٍ عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: أَخَذَ الْمُشْرِكُونَ عَمَّارَ بْنَ يَاسِرٍ فَلَمْ يَتْرُكُوهُ حَتَّى سَبَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَذَكَرَ آلِهَتَهُمْ بِخَيْرٍ ثُمَّ تَرَكُوهُ، فَلَمَّا أَتَى رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «مَا وَرَاءَكَ؟» قَالَ: شَرٌّ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، مَا تَرَكْتُ حَتَّى نِلْتُ مِنْكَ وَذَكَرْتُ آلِهَتَهُمْ بِخَيْرٍ. قَالَ: «كَيْفَ تَجِدُ قَلْبَكَ؟» قَالَ: مُطْمَئِنٌ بِالْإِيمَانِ. قَالَ: «إِنْ عَادُوا فَعُدْ». (الْمُسْتَدْرَكُ لِلْحَاكِمِ) وَجْهٌ: (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ فَإِذَا أَظْهَرَ ذَلِكَ وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَئِنٌ بِالْإِيمَانِ: عَنْ خَبَّابِ بْنِ الْأَرَتِّ قَالَ: شَكَوْنَا إِلَى رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَهُوَ مُتَوَسِّدٌ بُرْدَةً لَهُ فِي ظِلِّ الْكَعْبَةِ، فَقُلْنَا: أَلَا تَسْتَنْصِرُ لَنَا، أَلَا تَدْعُو لَنَا؟ فَقَالَ: قَدْ كَانَ مَنْ قَبْلَكُمْ، يُؤْخَذُ الرَّجُلُ فَيُحْفَرُ لَهُ فِي الْأَرْضِ فَيُجْعَلُ فِيهَا، فَيُجَاءُ بِالْمِنْشَارِ فَيُوضَعُ عَلَى رَأْسِهِ فَيُجْعَلُ نِصْفَيْنِ، وَيُمْشَطُ بِأَمْشَاطِ الْحَدِيدِ مَا دُونَ لَحْمِهِ وَعَظْمِهِ، فَمَا يَصُدُّهُ ذَلِكَ عَنْ دِينِهِ. (رَوَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ) أُصُولٌ: اگر کلمئہ کفر پر جبر کیا جائے بشر طیکہ دل ایمان پر مطمئن ہو تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
Book of Coercion. And if one is coerced into disbelief in Allah the Exalted or reviling the Prophet, peace be upon him, by imprisonment or chains or beating, that is not [valid] coercion until he is coerced by something he fears from it for his life or a limb. When he fears that, it is permissible for him to express what he is ordered to do. So when he expresses that while his heart is at peace with faith, there is no sin on him. And if he is patient until he is killed and does not express disbelief, he is rewardable. Directives: (1) The verse for establishing... (2) The hadith for establishing... (1) The hadith for establishing that when he expresses that while his heart is at peace with faith... Principles: If one is coerced into uttering a word of disbelief, provided the heart is at peace with faith, there is no harm.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Ikrah in al-Quduri states the ruling on coercion to commit kufr or revile the Prophet. The author first defines what constitutes ikrah (coercion): mere imprisonment, chains, or beating are not sufficient; the threat must be to life or limb. Only then is it permissible to outwardly comply. The heart must remain steadfast in faith; if so, no sin. If one endures to death, he earns reward. The author then provides proofs: the verse from Surah al-Nahl (16:106) explicitly permits verbal kufr under duress with a tranquil heart. The hadith of Ammar ibn Yasir shows the Prophet explicitly allowed him to repeat the words if coerced again. The hadith of Khabbab shows the high station of those who endure torture without recanting. The Urdu note summarizes: verbal kufr under duress with inner faith is no sin.

Key Terms
إكراه (ikrah): Coercion by threat of death or loss of limb that compels one to act against his will; lesser threats do not constitute valid ikrah.
مطمئن بالإيمان (mutma'innun bil iman): The heart is firm and at peace with faith, not affected by the outward utterance of disbelief.
سب النبي (sabb al-nabi): Reviling or insulting the Prophet Muhammad, which is normally kufr but under ikrah is permissible to utter outwardly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition is it permissible for a Muslim to utter words of disbelief under coercion according to the Hanafi school?
A) When threatened with imprisonment or beating.
B) When the coerced person's heart remains at peace with faith and the threat is to his life or limb.
C) Under any form of pressure, even without threat.
D) Only if the Prophet himself grants permission.

Key Takeaway
Under valid ikrah (threat to life or limb), a Muslim may utter words of disbelief without sin, provided the heart remains firm in iman; steadfastness to death earns great reward.

Coercion to Kill: The Ruling on Enduring Death Rather Than Killing an Innocent
Ruling that coercion does not permit murder; one must endure death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing under coercion, identify the proofs used, and distinguish liability between the coercer and the coerced.

Core Idea
Coercion does not permit killing an innocent; one must die rather than kill, and the coercer bears qisas.

This passage addresses the most severe moral and legal dilemma: being forced to kill another person under threat of your own death. The Hanafi school is categorical: you may not take the life of an innocent, even to save your own. The ruling establishes not only the sin and punishment of the coerced killer but also the unique liability of the coercer for qisas. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the proofs and the intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act? Coercing someone to kill another. The hukm for the coerced: it is haram to comply. He must remain patient and accept death.
The ruling applies only when coercion is by threat of death.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the Quranic verse (4:93) on intentional killing. This establishes the absolute prohibition without exception.
The verse is qati' al-thubut and qati' al-dalalah.
3
Analyse the liablity structure
The coerced killer is sinful and receives ta'zir, but qisas is on the coercer. The proof is the hadith of Abu Hurairah: 'The free commander is killed.'
This shows the coercer is the true cause.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Zufar holds the direct killer is solely liable. His proof is the statement of 'Ata: 'The killer is killed, not the commander.'
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the coercer faces qisas; under Zufar, the coerced killer faces qisas. This has serious practical implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ أُكْرِهَ بِقَتْلٍ عَلَى قَتْلِ غَيْرِهِ لَا يَسَعُهُ قَتْلُهُ بَلْ يَصْبِرُ حَتَّى يُقْتَلَ فَإِنْ قَتَلَهُ كَانَ آثِمًا وَيُعَزَّرُ وَالْقِصَاصُ عَلَى الَّذِي أَكْرَهَهُ إِنْ كَانَ الْقَتْلُ عَمْدًا. وَوَجْهٌ: (1) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ: {وَمَن يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِنًا مُّتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاؤُهُ جَهَنَّمُ خَالِدًا فِيهَا وَغَضِبَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَلَعَنَهُ وَأَعَدَّ لَهُ عَذَابًا عَظِيمًا} (سورة النِّسَاءِ: 93). وَوَجْهٌ: (1) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَيُعَزَّرُ وَالْقِصَاصُ عَلَى الَّذِي أَكْرَهَهُ: سَمِعْتُ أَبَا هُرَيْرَةَ يَقُولُ: «يُقْتَلُ الْحُرُّ الْآمِرُ، وَلَا يُقْتَلُ الْعَبْدُ». (مُصَنَّفُ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ) وَوَجْهٌ: (1) دَلِيلُ زُفَرَ: قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ: عَنْ عَطَاءٍ فِي رَجُلٍ أَمَرَ رَجُلًا حُرًّا فَقَتَلَ رَجُلًا قَالَ: «يُقْتَلُ الْقَاتِلُ، وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الْآمِرِ شَيْءٌ». (مُصَنَّفُ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ)
And if one is coerced by [threat of] death into killing another, it is not permissible for him to kill him; rather, he should be patient until he himself is killed. If he kills him, he is sinful and is subjected to discretionary punishment (ta'zir), and the retaliation (qisas) is upon the one who coerced him, if the killing was intentional. A directive: (1) The verse for establishing: 'And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding eternally therein, and Allah has become angry with him and has cursed him and has prepared for him a great punishment.' (Surah an-Nisa: 93). A directive: (1) The saying of a Companion for establishing that ta'zir and qisas are upon the coercer: I heard Abu Hurairah say: 'The free commander [coercer] is killed, and the slave is not killed.' A directive: (1) Proof of Zufar: The saying of a Tabi'i: 'Ata' regarding a man who ordered a free man to kill a man, said: The killer is killed, and nothing is upon the commander.'
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage addresses the most severe form of coercion: being forced to kill an innocent person under threat of one's own death. The ruling is categorical: it is impermissible to comply. The coerced person must endure his own death rather than kill another. If he does kill, he commits a sin and receives ta'zir. However, the qisas (retaliation) falls upon the coercer (the one who issued the threat) if the killing was intentional. The author provides proofs: the Quranic verse declaring severe punishment for intentional killing. The saying of Abu Hurairah indicates that the one who commands (the coercer) is liable for qisas, while the coerced executor (if a slave) is not killed? The text says 'the free commander is killed' implying the coercer is subject to qisas. The author also mentions Zufar's argument that the direct killer is solely liable, but the Hanafi position is that the coercer is the true killer due to duress. Note: The passage includes a minority view (Zufar's) but the mufta bihi is that the coercer bears qisas if he compelled intentionally.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment of death for intentional murder, applied to the person legally deemed the killer.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment left to the judge's discretion, applied here to the coerced killer for committing a forbidden act.
إكراه (ikrah): Coercion or duress that negates free will when it involves threat of death or severe harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on a person who, under threat of death, kills another innocent person?
A) He is excused because of coercion, no sin.
B) He is sinful and receives ta'zir, but qisas is on the coercer.
C) Both the coercer and the coerced are liable for qisas.
D) The coerced is liable for qisas because he physically did the killing.

Key Takeaway
Under Hanafi law, coercion to kill does not justify the act; one must endure death, and the coercer is liable for qisas.

Coercion to Kill: Liability of the Coercer vs. the Coerced
States the Hanafi ruling on coercion to kill and provides evidence, including an intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on coercion to kill, distinguish the liabilities of the coercer and the coerced, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar.

Core Idea
Under coercion, the killer sins and receives tazir, but qisas falls on the coercer.

This lesson examines a critical fiqh issue: what happens when a person is forced under threat of death to kill another? The Hanafi school holds that the coerced must not kill, and if they do, they are sinful but the retribution is on the coercer. We will explore the evidence from Quran, hadith, and an intra-Hanafi disagreement with Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act of killing under coercion. Determine the ruling for the coerced person: is it permissible or not?
The text clearly states it is not permissible (la yasa'uhu).
2
Identify liabilities
Who bears the burdens: sin (ithm), discretionary punishment (ta'zir), and retribution (qisas)? Distinguish between the coerced and the coercer.
The coerced is sinful and gets tazir; the coercer bears qisas if the killing was intentional.
3
Locate the Hanafi proof
What evidence does the Hanafi school cite? Identify the hadith of Abu Hurairah and understand how it supports the ruling.
The hadith: 'The free commander is killed, and the slave is not killed.'
4
Identify the opposing view
Zufar, a Hanafi scholar, disagrees. What is his evidence? It is a statement of 'Ata (a Tabi'i).
Zufar's proof: 'The killer is killed, and the commander is not liable.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence of this difference? How does it affect who is executed?
Hanafi: coercer executed; Zufar: coerced killer executed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الإِكْرَامِ
القدوري مع احاديثه ١٠ وَإِنْ أُكْرِهَ بِقَتْلِ عَلَى قَتْلِ غَيْرِهِ لَا يَسَعُهُ قَتْلُهُ بَلْ يَصْبِرُ حَتَّى يَقْتُلَ فَإِنْ قَتَلَهُ كَانَ آثِماً وَيُعَزَّرُ وَالْقِصَاصُ عَلَى الَّذِي أَكْرَهَهُ إِنْ كَانَ الْقَتْلُ عَمْدًا
الْمَيْتَةَ وَالدَّمَ وَلَحْمَ الْخِنزِيرِ وَمَا أُهِلَّ بِهِ لِغَيْرِ اللَّهِ فَمَنِ اضْطُرَّ غَيْرَ بَاغٍ وَلَا عَادٍ فَلَا إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ إِنَّ اللَّهَ غَفُورٌ رَّحِيمٌ (سورة البقرة، 2 آيت نمبر (173)
وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَإِنْ أُكْرِهَ بِقَتْلِ عَلَى قَتْلِ غَيْرِهِ و وَمَن يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِنًا مُّتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاؤُهُ جَهَنَّمُ خَالِدًا فِيهَا وَغَضِبَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَلَعَنَهُ وَأَعَدَّ لَهُ عَذَابًا عَظِيمًا ) (سورة النساء، 4 آيت نمبر (93)
الوجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيُعَزَّرُ وَالْقِصَاصُ عَلَى الَّذِي أَكْرَهَهُ \ سَمِعْتُ أَبَا هُرَيْرَةَ يَقُولُ: «يُقْتَلُ الْحُرُ الْآمِرَ، وَلَا يُقْتَلُ الْعَبْدُ»، أَرَأَيْتَ أَبُو هُرَيْرَةَ الْقَائِلُ: «لَوْ أَنَّ رَجُلًا أَرْسَلَ بِهَدِيَّةٍ، مَعَ عَبْدِهِ إِلَى رَجُلٍ مَنْ أَهْدَاهَا؟»، (مصنف عبد الرزاق بَابُ الَّذِي يَأْمُرُ عَبْدَهُ فَيُقْتَلُ رَجُلًا، غمبر 17888)
وجه (۱) دليل زفر قول التابعى لثبوت وَيُعَزَّرُ وَالْقِصَاصُ عَلَى الَّذِي أَكْرَهَهُ \ عَنْ عَطَاءٍ فِي رَجُلٍ أَمَرَ رَجُلًا حُرًّا فَقَتَلَ رَجُلًا قَالَ: «يُقْتَلُ الْقَاتِلُ، وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الْآمِرِ شَيْءٌ»(مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ الَّذِي يَأْمُرُ عَبْدَهُ فَيُقْتَلُ رَجُلًا، نمبر 17882)
And if he is coerced by threat of killing to kill another, it is not permissible for him to kill him, rather he should be patient until he is killed. So if he kills him, he is sinful and is punished with tazir, and qisas is upon the one who coerced him if the killing was intentional.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on a person coerced under threat of death to kill someone else. The coerced person may not commit the murder; he must endure the threat. If he does kill, he becomes sinful and receives a discretionary punishment (tazir), but the retribution (qisas) falls on the coercer if the killing was intentional. The text then provides proofs: the Quranic verse 2:173 which permits eating carrion under necessity but does not permit killing, indicating that killing another is not allowed even under coercion; verse 4:93 which threatens eternal punishment for intentional murder; the hadith of Abu Hurairah that the free commander is killed and not the slave; and finally the view of Zufar who cites the statement of Ata that only the killer is executed and the commander is not liable. This represents an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa holds the coercer liable, while Zufar holds only the killer liable. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
إكراه (ikrah): Compelling someone to do an act against their will under threat
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment determined by the judge for sins that have no fixed hadd
قصاص (qisas): Retributive justice, specifically the death penalty for intentional killing

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a person who kills another under coercion?
A) He is free of sin
B) He is sinful and receives tazir
C) He faces qisas
D) He is not punished

Key Takeaway
Under Hanafi fiqh, the one who coerces another to kill bears the qisas, while the coerced killer is sinful and receives tazir.

Peace Treaties with the Enemy in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on Imam's authority to make peace with enemy for benefit of Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on peace treaties with the enemy and explain its basis in the Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
A peace treaty with the enemy is permissible when the Imam determines it benefits the Muslims.

Al-Quduri states a clear ruling: the Imam may make peace with the enemy or a faction of them if there is benefit for the Muslims. This lesson unpacks that ruling, its condition of maslahah (public benefit), and the textual evidences provided in the sharh: a Qur'anic verse and two hadiths from the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah. By the end, you will not only know the ruling but also understand how the Hanafi school derives a general permissibility from these proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the matn sentence: 'Wa idha ra'a al-imam an yusaliha ahl al-harb... fala ba'sa bihi.' Identify the legal category: is it wajib, mandub, mubah? Note the phrase 'fala ba'sa bihi' indicates permissibility (ibahah). The Hanafi position is mubah, not obligatory or recommended.
2
Isolate the Condition
The ruling is conditional: 'wa kana fi dhalika maslahatun li al-muslimeen.' Recognize that maslahah is the operative condition. In Hanafi fiqh, the Imam's discretion is guided by public interest. Contrast with schools that may require the treaty to be temporary or only upon enemy request.
The condition is not the enemy's request; it is the presence of benefit.
3
Analyze the Quranic Evidence
The sharh cites Surah al-Anfal (8:61). Note that the imperative 'fajnah laha' follows a conditional clause ('in janahu'). According to Hanafi usul, an amr after a condition indicates ibahah (permission), not wujub. This is the key derivation: the verse does not obligate peace, but permits it when the enemy inclines.
The dalala is zanni because of the condition, even though thubut is qat'i.
4
Examine the Prophetic Evidence
The sharh presents the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah. The Prophet made peace with the Quraysh on terms that some companions found unfavorable. This shows that peace is permissible even if it involves concessions, as long as the overall maslahah is served. The hadiths confirm the principle and provide a concrete precedent.
The treaty included a ten-year truce, demonstrating that long-term peace is allowed.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi Position
Combine the ruling, condition, and evidence. The Hanafi school holds that making peace with the enemy is fundamentally mubah, contingent on the Imam's assessment of maslahah. This flexibility is rooted in the Quranic verse and the Prophet's practice. Recognize that this is a mukhtalaf fih issue: other schools may require stricter conditions (e.g., the treaty must be limited in duration or only if necessary).
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is the broad discretion of the Imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا رَأَى الْإِمَامُ أَنْ يُصَالِحَ أَهْلَ الْحَرْبِ أَوْ فَرِيقًا مِنْهُمْ وَكَانَ فِي ذَلِكَ مَصْلَحَةٌ لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ فَلَا بَأْسَ بِهِ.
وجه : (1) الآية لثبوت وَإِذَا رَأَى الْإِمَامُ أَنْ يُصَالِحَ أَهْلَ الْحَرْبِ ﴿وَإِن جَنَحُواْ لِلسَّلْمِ فَاجْنَحْ لَهَا وَتَوَكَّلْ عَلَى اللَّهِ إِنَّهُ هُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْعَلِيمُ﴾ (سورة الانفال، 8 أيت، نمبر 61).
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا رَأَى الْإِمَامُ أَنْ يُصَالِحَ أَهْلَ الْحَرْبِ عَنِ الْمِسْوَرِ بْنِ مَخْرَمَةَ وَمَرْوَانَ، يُصَدِّقُ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا حَدِيثَ صَاحِبِهِ، قَالَا: «خَرَجَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم زَمَنَ الْحَدَيْبِيَةِ ... لا يَسْأَلُونِي خُطَّةَ يُعَظِمُونَ فِيهَا حُرُمَاتِ اللهِ إِلَّا أَعْطَيْتُهُمْ إِيَّاهَا فَقَالَ لَهُ النَّبِيُّ : عَلَى أَنْ تُخَلُّوا بَيْنَنَا وَبَيْنَ الْبَيْتِ فَنَطُوفَ بِهِ... فَلَمَّا فَرَغَ مِنْ قَضِيَّةِ الْكِتَابِ، قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لِأَصْحَابِهِ : قُومُوا فَالْخَرُوا ثُمَّ احْلِقُوا، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ الشَّرُوطِ فِي الْجِهَادِ وَالْمُصَاحَةِ مَعَ أَهْلِ الْخَرْبِ وَكِتَابَةِ الشُّرُوطِ، نمبر 2731/ مسلم شريف، باب صُلْحِ الْحَدَيْبِيَّةِ فِي الخُدَيْبِيَةِ نمبر 1783).
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا رَأَى الْإِمَامُ أَنْ يُصَالِحَ أَهْلَ الْحَرْبِ عَنِ الْمِسْوَرِ بْنِ مَخْرَمَةَ، وَمَرْوَانَ بْنِ الْحَكَمِ، «أَنَّهُمْ اصْطَلَحُوا عَلَى وَضْعِ الْحَرْبِ عَشْرَ سِنِينَ، يَأْمَنُ فِيهِنَّ النَّاسُ وَعَلَى أَنَّ بَيْنَنَا عَيْبَةً مَكْفُوفَةٌ، وَأَنَّهُ لَا إِسْلَالَ وَلَا إِغْلَالَ، (سنن ابوداود بَابٌ فِي صُلْحِ الْعَدُوّ، نمبر 1766).
And when the Imam sees (finds it appropriate) to make peace with the people of war or a group among them, and there is benefit for the Muslims in that, then there is no harm in it. Evidence (1): The aayah for establishing 'And when the Imam sees to make peace with the people of war': {And if they incline to peace, then incline to it and rely upon Allah. Indeed, He is the Hearing, the Knowing.} (Surah al-Anfal, verse 61). Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing 'And when the Imam sees to make peace with the people of war': from al-Miswar bin Makhramah and Marwan, each confirming the other's narration: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, went out at the time of al-Hudaybiyyah... They do not ask me for a plan by which they honor the sacred things of Allah except that I give it to them.' The Prophet said to him: 'On condition that you allow us to go to the House (Kaaba) and circumambulate it...' When he finished writing the treaty, the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said to his companions: 'Arise, slaughter (the sacrificial animals) and then shave (your heads).' (Bukhari, Book of Conditions in Jihad and Reconciliation with the People of War and Writing Conditions, no. 2731; Muslim, Book of the Treaty of al-Hudaybiyyah, no. 1783). Evidence (3): The hadith for establishing 'And when the Imam sees to make peace with the people of war': from al-Miswar bin Makhramah and Marwan bin al-Hakam: 'They made peace on condition of laying down war for ten years, during which people would be safe, and that between us there would be an unopened covenant, and that there would be no secret theft or open plunder.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Book of Peace with the Enemy, no. 1766).
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Quduri, followed by a sharh (commentary) providing proofs. The ruling: The Imam (leader of the Muslims) has the authority to enter into a peace treaty with the people of war (non-Muslim belligerents) or a group of them, provided it serves the general benefit of the Muslims. The phrase 'fala ba'sa bihi' indicates permissibility (ibahah) in the Hanafi school. The commentary then provides three proofs: first, a Qur'anic verse commanding peace if the enemy inclines to it; second, the incident of the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah where the Prophet made peace with the Quraysh; third, another narration detailing the ten-year truce. These establish the legal basis for such treaties. The Hanafi position is that peace is permissible when beneficial, but not an obligation; the Imam uses his discretion.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A peace treaty or reconciliation between the Muslim leader and the enemy belligerents.
أهل الحرب (ahl al-harb): Non-Muslims with whom Muslims are in a state of war (dar al-harb).
مصلحة (maslahah): Benefit or public interest that the Imam assesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition may the Imam make a peace treaty with the people of war according to Al-Quduri?
A) Only if the enemy requests peace first
B) If there is a clear benefit for the Muslims
C) Only if the treaty lasts less than ten years
D) Only if no alternative exists

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, peace treaties with the enemy are fundamentally mubah, conditional on the Imam's assessment of public benefit (maslahah), as established by the Quran and the Prophet's practice at Hudaybiyyah.

Breaking a Peace Treaty: Notification Required
Ruling on Imam's obligation to notify enemy before breaking a treaty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on breaking a peace treaty and explain the requirement of prior notice (nadh) using Quran and hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Breaking a peace treaty requires prior notice; otherwise it is treachery.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses a critical question in Islamic international law: Can a Muslim leader break a peace treaty before its term? The Hanafi ruling is clear: the Imam must formally notify the enemy (nadh) before attacking. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, and explains why notification is obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is breaking a peace treaty before its term. The ruling is that it is permissible but only with prior notice (nadh).
The notification is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Surah al-Anfal (8):58 commands: 'And if you fear from a people treachery, then throw (their treaty) back to them equally.' The imperative 'fanbidh' indicates obligation.
The verse addresses the case where treachery is feared.
3
Locate the Hadith proof
The hadith of 'Amr bin 'Abasah forbids undoing a treaty until its term expires or notice is given equally.
The hadith explicitly prohibits treachery.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the imperative form indicates wujub. 'Ala sawa'' ensures both parties are informed equally.
This is why notification is wajib, not just recommended.
5
Apply the ruling
The Imam must give formal notice before attacking; otherwise the attack is haram (ghadr).
This applies even if breaking early is seen as beneficial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ صَالحَهُمْ مُدَّةً ثُمَّ رَأَى أَنَّ نَقْضَ الصُّلْحِ أَنْفَعَ نَبَذَ إِلَيْهِمْ وَقَاتَلَهُمْ.
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ صَاحَهُمْ مُدَّةَ ﴿وَإِمَّا تَخَافَنَّ مِن قَوْمٍ خِيَانَةَ فَأَنْبِذْ إِلَيْهِمْ عَلَى سَوَاءٍ إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يُحِبُّ الْخَاسِنِينَ) (سورة الانفال، 8 آيت نمبر 58).
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ صَاحَهُمْ مُدَّةً سَمِعْتُ سُلَيْمَ بْنَ عَامِرٍ، يَقُولُ: كَانَ بَيْنَ مُعَاوِيَةَ وَبَيْنَ أَهْلِ الرُّومِ عَهْدٌ، وَكَانَ يَسِيرُ فِي بِلَادِهِمْ، حَتَّى إِذَا انْقَضَى العَهْدُ أَغَارَ عَلَيْهِمْ، فَإِذَا رَجُلٌ عَلَى دَابَّةٍ أَوْ عَلَى فَرَسٍ، وَهُوَ يَقُولُ: اللَّهُ أَكْبَرُ، وَفَاء لَا غَدْرٌ، وَإِذَا هُوَ عَمْرُو بْنُ عَبَسَةَ، فَسَأَلَهُ مُعَاوِيَةُ عَنْ ذَلِكَ، فَقَالَ : سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ: «مَنْ كَانَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ قَوْمٍ عَهْدٌ فَلَا يَكُلَّنَّ عَهْدًا، وَلَا يَشُدَّنَّهُ حَتَّى يَمْضِيَ أَمَدُهُ أَوْ يَنْبِدَ إِلَيْهِمْ عَلَى سَوَاءٍ»، قَالَ: فَرَجَعَ مُعَاوِيَةُ بِالنَّاسِ،(سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الغَدْرِ، نمبر 1580 سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الْإِمَامِ يَكُونُ بَيْنَهُ، وَبَيْنَ الْعَدُةِ عَهْدٌ فَيَسِيرُ إِلَيْهِ، نمبر 2759).
If he made peace with them for a duration, then he sees that breaking the peace is more beneficial, he should cast (the treaty) to them (i.e., give notice) and fight them. Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing 'if he made peace with them for a duration': {And if you fear from a people treachery, then throw (their treaty) back to them equally. Indeed, Allah does not like the treacherous.} (Surah al-Anfal, verse 58). Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing 'if he made peace with them for a duration': I heard Sulaym bin 'Amir say: There was a treaty between Mu'awiyah and the people of Rome, and he was marching in their lands. When the treaty expired, he raided them. Then a man on a horse was saying: Allahu Akbar! Fulfillment, not treachery! That was 'Amr bin 'Abasah. Mu'awiyah asked him about it, and he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say: 'Whoever has a treaty between him and a people, let him not undo the treaty nor strengthen it (i.e., bind himself) until its term expires, or he throws (it) back to them equally.' So Mu'awiyah returned with the people. (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Book of Treachery, no. 1580; Sunan Abi Dawud, Book of the Imam who has a treaty between him and the enemy and marches to him, no. 2759).
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a second ruling from the matn, with its proofs. The ruling: If the Imam has made a peace treaty for a fixed term, and later concludes that breaking the treaty is more beneficial for the Muslims, he may not simply attack without warning. He must 'cast' (yambidh) the treaty back to them, i.e., formally notify them that the treaty is terminated, and then fight. The proof is from the Qur'anic verse which commands that if treachery is feared, the treaty should be 'thrown back equally' — meaning they should be informed so that both parties are on equal footing. The second proof is a hadith forbidding treachery and requiring either waiting until the term expires or giving notice. The Hanafi school emphasizes this as wajib (obligatory) to avoid treachery (ghadr). The Urud summary at the bottom of the page reiterates this principle.

Key Terms
نبذ (nadh): Formally casting back the treaty, i.e., giving notice of termination.
نقض الصلح (naqd al-sulh): Breaking or annulling a peace treaty before its term ends.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must the Imam do before breaking a peace treaty according to this passage?
A) Wait for the enemy to break it first
B) Give formal notice to the enemy (nadh)
C) Consult the scholars
D) Leave the treaty as is

Key Takeaway
Before breaking a peace treaty, the Imam must give formal notice (nadh) to the enemy; otherwise, it is treachery prohibited in Islam.
